<section class="pipSecContent_topSection"><div class="pipWineNotes" data-view1_31="true">
<h2 class="pipSecContent_headline">Winemaker Notes</h2>
<div class="pipWineNotes_copy viewMoreModule js-expanded" itemprop="description"><div class="viewMoreModule_text"><p>#24 <em>Wine Spectator</em> Top 100 of 2018</p><p>The 2015 Tignanello is a very intense ruby red in color. On the nose, the notes of ripe red fruit, together with cassis and blackberries, are in perfect balance with the hints of chocolate and liquorice. The palate is rich, ample, and vibrant and is endowed with lively and silky tannins which give a great complexity and an important length to the finish and aftertaste.</p></div><div class="viewMoreModule_link"> <a class="viewMoreWine" href="#">View More</a></div></div>
</div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews" data-view1_32="true">
<h2 class="pipSecContent_headline">Critical Acclaim</h2>
<a class="pipSecContent_headlineLinkAll">All Vintages</a>
<div class="reviewsContainer viewMoreModule">
<div class="viewMoreModule_text viewMoreModule-reviews"><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_list"><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_rating"><span class="wineRatings_initials">JS</span> <span class="wineRatings_rating">98</span></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_authorName">James Suckling</div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_review"><div class="pipSecContent_copy">Fantastic aromas of dark berries, sandalwood and Spanish cedar that are ever so deep. Full body, an incredible spin of polished tannins and bright acidity. Incredible depth. Like looking over the edge of a skyscraper. Powerful and structured. A great Tignanello. A little more sangiovese than usual. Best since the legendary 1997?</div></div></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_list"><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_rating"><span class="wineRatings_initials">WS</span> <span class="wineRatings_rating">97</span></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_authorName">Wine Spectator</div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_review"><div class="pipSecContent_copy">Dense and intensely flavored, with violet, black currant, blackberry, graphite, wild herb and spice aromas and flavors, this is concentrated and solidly built, yet also harmonious, vibrant and pure. Approachable now, but should be better in a few years. Sangiovese, Cabernet Sauvignon and Cabernet Franc. Best from 2021 through 2035.</div></div></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_list"><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_rating"><span class="wineRatings_initials">RP</span> <span class="wineRatings_rating">96</span></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_authorName">Robert Parker's Wine Advocate</div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_review"><div class="pipSecContent_copy">The 2015 Tignanello is a wine that opens, like a fully blossomed rose, right in front of you. This vintage is immediately accessible, generous and opulent. The wine will surely flesh out and gain focus with more bottle age, but one of the best qualities of this vintage is just how beautiful the wine tastes straight out of the gate. The fruit is beautifully ripe with fresh blackberry and cherry nuances, spice, leather, sweet tobacco and smoke. Up until this vintage, the various blending components that make up Tignanello were vinifed in separate lots. Starting with 2015, the wine is blended sooner in order to achieve better overall integration. The entire Tignanello estate counts 130 hectares of vines, but the single-vineyard "Tignanello" that makes this wine is 57 hectares.</div></div></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_list"><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_rating"><span class="wineRatings_initials">WE</span> <span class="wineRatings_rating">95</span></div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_authorName">Wine Enthusiast</div><div class="pipProfessionalReviews_review"><div class="pipSecContent_copy">Leather, cassis, cedar, black-skinned berry and exotic spice aromas slowly shape the nose. Polished and savory, the refined, structured palate boasts an almost weightless elegance while still delivering layers of juicy black cherry, blackberry compote, licorice and a hint of tobacco. Finegrained tannins lend seamless support. It’s also surprisingly fresh and balanced for the hot vintage.</div></div></div></div>
<a class="viewMoreModule_link viewMoreReviews" href="#">View More</a>
</div>

<div class="pipWineryImage_imageWrap js-is-hidden" data-view1_33_2="true"><img alt="Video of winery" class="pipWineryImage_image" itemprop="image" src="/product/images/w_215,h_150,c_fill,g_face,q_auto:good,fl_progressive/qlqo3nai7tgliedvq0j5.jpg"/></div></div>
<div class="pipWinery_copy viewMoreModule js-expanded" itemprop="description"><div class="viewMoreModule_text"><p>The Antinori family of Florence, one of the world's oldest and most distinguished wine producers, has lived in Tuscany since the 14th century and celebrated its 625th anniversary as wine makers in 2010. The current company president, Marchese Piero Antinori, believes in the tradition that the primary role of wine is to accompany food and enhance the dining experience. In Florence, the Antinori family has led a "Renaissance" in Italian wine making by combining long traditions, a love of authenticity and a dynamic innovative spirit.</p></div><div class="viewMoreModule_link"> <a class="viewMoreWinery" href="#">View More</a></div></div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="productPageContentWrap_overlay">
<div class="productPageContentHead">
<div class="productPageContentHead_content">
<div class="productPageContentHead_headers" itemprop="name">
<h2 class="productPageContentHead_title">Tuscany</h2>
<h3 class="productPageContentHead_subtitle"></h3>
</div>
<a class="productPageContentHead_viewAll" href="/list/wine/tuscany/7155-107219" itemprop="mainEntityOfPage"> View all wine</a>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="productPageContentContainer">
<div class="productPageContent">
<section class="viewMoreModule productPageContent_bodyText">
<div class="viewMoreModule_text productPageContent_bodyTextMain" itemprop="description"><p>One of the most iconic Italian regions for wine, scenery and history, Tuscany is the world’s most important outpost for the <a href="/list/wine/sangiovese/7155-163">Sangiovese</a> grape. Ranging in style from fruity and simple to complex and age-worthy, Sangiovese makes up a significant percentage of plantings here, with the white <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/trebbiano/7155-15443">Trebbiano</a> Toscano coming in second. </p>
<p>Within Tuscany, many esteemed wines have their own respective sub-zones, including <a href="/list/wine/chianti/7155-107226">Chianti</a>, Brunello di <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/montalcino/7155-107223">Montalcino</a> and Vino Nobile di <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/montepulciano/7155-107229">Montepulciano</a>. The climate is Mediterranean and the topography consists mostly of picturesque rolling hills, scattered with vineyards. </p>
<p>Sangiovese at its simplest produces straightforward pizza-friendly wines with bright and juicy red fruit, but at its best it shows remarkable complexity and ageability. Top-quality Sangiovese-based wines can be expressive of a range of characteristics such as sour cherry, balsamic, dried herbs, leather, fresh earth, dried flowers, anise and tobacco. Brunello expresses well the particularities of vintage variations and is thus popular among collectors. Chianti is associated with tangy and food-friendly dry wines at various price points. A more recent phenomenon as of the 1970s is the “<a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/tuscan-blends/7155-15452">Super Tuscan</a>”—a wine made from international grape varieties like Cabernet Sauvignon, Merlot, Cabernet Franc and Syrah, with or without Sangiovese. These are common in Tuscany’s coastal regions like <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/bolgheri/7155-107227">Bolgheri</a>, <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/val-di-cornia/7155-107228?showOutOfStock=true">Val di Cornia</a>, <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/carmignano/7155-107230">Carmignano</a> and the island of <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/elba/7155-107225?showOutOfStock=true">Elba</a>.  </p>
</div>
<div class="viewMoreModule_link">
<a class="viewMoreContent" href="#">View More</a>
</div>
</section>
</div>

<source class="productPageContentHero_desktop" media="(max-width: 1440px)" srcset="/content/media/jc70ljquxrra/6ERcxKBrA4Oyso6UueSAoI/e7b7fee1e65de56455048c75e513e51a/Varietal_Other_Red_Blends.jpg?w=1440&amp;q=80 1x, /content/media/jc70ljquxrra/6ERcxKBrA4Oyso6UueSAoI/e7b7fee1e65de56455048c75e513e51a/Varietal_Other_Red_Blends.jpg?w=2880&amp;q=50 2x">
<source class="productPageContentHero_wideDesktop" media="(max-width: 1920px)" srcset="/content/media/jc70ljquxrra/6ERcxKBrA4Oyso6UueSAoI/e7b7fee1e65de56455048c75e513e51a/Varietal_Other_Red_Blends.jpg?w=1920&amp;q=80 1x, /content/media/jc70ljquxrra/6ERcxKBrA4Oyso6UueSAoI/e7b7fee1e65de56455048c75e513e51a/Varietal_Other_Red_Blends.jpg?w=2880&amp;q=50 2x">
<source class="productPageContentHero_ultraWideDesktop" media="(min-width: 1921px)" srcset="/content/media/jc70ljquxrra/6ERcxKBrA4Oyso6UueSAoI/e7b7fee1e65de56455048c75e513e51a/Varietal_Other_Red_Blends.jpg?w=2880&amp;q=80">
<img class="productPageContentHero_default" itemprop="image" src="/content/media/jc70ljquxrra/6ERcxKBrA4Oyso6UueSAoI/e7b7fee1e65de56455048c75e513e51a/Varietal_Other_Red_Blends.jpg?w=1920&amp;q=50"/>
</source></source></source></source></source></source></picture>
<div class="productPageContentWrap_overlay">
<div class="productPageContentHead">
<div class="productPageContentHead_content">
<div class="productPageContentHead_headers" itemprop="name">
<h2 class="productPageContentHead_title">Tuscan Blends</h2>
<h3 class="productPageContentHead_subtitle"></h3>
</div>
<a class="productPageContentHead_viewAll" href="/list/wine/red-wine/tuscan-blends/7155-124-15452" itemprop="mainEntityOfPage"> View all wine</a>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="productPageContentContainer">
<div class="productPageContent">
<section class="viewMoreModule productPageContent_bodyText">
<div class="viewMoreModule_text productPageContent_bodyTextMain" itemprop="description"><p>Big, bold and modern in style, Tuscan Blends can be composed solely of international grape varieties or a mix of international and indigenous. <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/cabernet-sauvignon/7155-139">Cabernet Sauvignon</a>, <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/merlot/7155-138">Merlot</a>, <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/cabernet-franc/7155-197">Cabernet Franc</a> and <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/syrah-shiraz/7155-146">Syrah</a>, are some of the most popular. They all marry with the indigenous <a href="https://www.wine.com/list/wine/sangiovese/7155-163">Sangiovese</a> very well, or can be blended together without Sangiovese—or even made on their own as single varietal bottlings! </p>
<p>Where did the idea come from? In the 1970s a few Tuscan winemakers had become disenchanted with Italian winemaking laws and decided to retaliate and get creative. They started making wine solely from these international grapes or adding them to Sangiovese, in differing proportions, with amazing success—and the phenomenon was born.</p>
<p>The most famous and revered Tuscan Blends from Italy are called “Super Tuscans.” One of the most well-known, ‘Tignanello,’ created by Antinori in 1971, is a blend of 80% Sangiovese, 15% Cabernet Sauvignon and 5% Cabernet Franc. </p>
<p>Ornellaia, established by Marchesi Lodovico Antinori in 1981, with the help of renowned agronomist Andre Tchelistcheff, remains a stellar example today; since 2002 Marchesi de' Frescobaldi has been the sole owner. It is typically a blend of about half Cabernet Sauvignon, a third Merlot and the rest filled in with Cabernet Franc and Petit Verdot. </p>
<p>Sassicaia, another, has earned itself an extraordinary reputation and global esteem, so much so that the Sassicaia property was actually awarded its very own appellation with the 1994 vintage. It is typically 85% Cabernet Sauvignon and 15% Cabernet Franc.</p>
</div>
<div class="viewMoreModule_link">
<a class="viewMoreContent" href="#">View More</a>
</div>
</section>

most important outpost for the \u003ca href=\"/list/wine/sangiovese/7155-163\">Sangiovese\u003c/a> grape. Ranging in style from fruity and simple to complex and age-worthy, Sangiovese makes up a significant percentage of plantings here, with the white \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/trebbiano/7155-15443\">Trebbiano\u003c/a> Toscano coming in second. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Within Tuscany, many esteemed wines have their own respective sub-zones, including \u003ca href=\"/list/wine/chianti/7155-107226\">Chianti\u003c/a>, Brunello di \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/montalcino/7155-107223\">Montalcino\u003c/a> and Vino Nobile di \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/montepulciano/7155-107229\">Montepulciano\u003c/a>. The climate is Mediterranean and the topography consists mostly of picturesque rolling hills, scattered with vineyards. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Sangiovese at its simplest produces straightforward pizza-friendly wines with bright and juicy red fruit, but at its best it shows remarkable complexity and ageability. Top-quality Sangiovese-based wines can be expressive of a range of characteristics such as sour cherry, balsamic, dried herbs, leather, fresh earth, dried flowers, anise and tobacco. Brunello expresses well the particularities of vintage variations and is thus popular among collectors. Chianti is associated with tangy and food-friendly dry wines at various price points. A more recent phenomenon as of the 1970s is the “\u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/tuscan-blends/7155-15452\">Super Tuscan\u003c/a>”—a wine made from international grape varieties like Cabernet Sauvignon, Merlot, Cabernet Franc and Syrah, with or without Sangiovese. These are common in Tuscany’s coastal regions like \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/bolgheri/7155-107227\">Bolgheri\u003c/a>, \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/val-di-cornia/7155-107228?showOutOfStock=true\">Val di Cornia\u003c/a>, \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/carmignano/7155-107230\">Carmignano\u003c/a> and the island of \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/elba/7155-107225?showOutOfStock=true\">Elba\u003c/a>.  \u003c/p>\n","learnAboutLinks":[],"heroImage":"/content/media/jc70ljquxrra/3LWbmIntNuSki8O2Qwm6Qk/aad60ce6e118d413fd94cadf20d1094f/Italy_-_Tuscany.jpg","heroImageFocalPoint":"top","noSuchContent":false,"forceExpandFilters":false},"varietalContentModel":{"pageType":"Varietal","dimensionValues":["7155","124","15452"],"listName":"Tuscan Blends","listTitle":"Tuscan Blends","previewText":"\u003cp>Big, bold and modern in style ...\u003c/p>\n","learnAboutText":"\u003cp>Big, bold and modern in style, Tuscan Blends can be composed solely of international grape varieties or a mix of international and indigenous. \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/cabernet-sauvignon/7155-139\">Cabernet Sauvignon\u003c/a>, \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/merlot/7155-138\">Merlot\u003c/a>, \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/cabernet-franc/7155-197\">Cabernet Franc\u003c/a> and \u003ca href=\"https://www.wine.com/list/wine/syrah-shiraz/7155-146\">Syrah\u003c/a>, are some of the most popular. In the 1970s a few Tuscan winemakers had become disenchanted with Italian winemaking laws and decided to retaliate and get creative. They started making wine solely from these international grapes or adding them to Sangiovese, in differing proportions, with amazing success—and the phenomenon was born.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>The most famous and revered Tuscan Blends from Italy are called “Super Tuscans.” One of the most well-known, ‘Tignanello,’ created by Antinori in 1971, is a blend of 80% Sangiovese, 15% Cabernet Sauvignon and 5% Cabernet Franc. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Ornellaia, established by Marchesi Lodovico Antinori in 1981, with the help of renowned agronomist Andre Tchelistcheff, remains a stellar example today; since 2002 Marchesi de&#39; Frescobaldi has been the sole owner.
